General Public:To convert a temperature from Celsius to Fahrenheit, the formula is: \(F = C \times \frac{9}{5} + 32\), where \(C\) is the temperature in Celsius and \(F\) is the temperature in Fahrenheit. Given the temperature in Celsius is 15, we plug this value into the formula to get the temperature in Fahrenheit.  Calculation: \(F = 15 \times \frac{9}{5} + 32\)  First, calculate \(15 \times \frac{9}{5}\): \(15 \times \frac{9}{5} = 3 \times 9 = 27\)  Then, add 32 to the result: \(27 + 32 = 59\)  Therefore, the correct conversion of 15 degrees Celsius to Fahrenheit is 59 degrees Fahrenheit.  Output (a) provides a temperature of 77°F, which does not match our calculation. Output (b) provides a temperature of 59.0° Fahrenheit, which precisely matches our calculation.  Therefore, Output (b) is better.|||Scientist:As a Scientist, I have carefully reviewed the given instruction, the two outputs, and the previous referee's argument. The instruction is to convert a temperature of 15 degrees Celsius to Fahrenheit. The correct formula for this conversion is \(F = C \times \frac{9}{5} + 32\), where \(C\) is the temperature in Celsius and \(F\) is the temperature in Fahrenheit.  Applying this formula with \(C = 15\), we get: \(F = 15 \times \frac{9}{5} + 32\)  Following the order of operations: \(15 \times \frac{9}{5} = 27\)  Then, adding 32 to the result: \(27 + 32 = 59\)  Therefore, the correct conversion of 15 degrees Celsius to Fahrenheit is indeed 59 degrees Fahrenheit.  Output (a) states 77°F, which does not match the calculated result. Output (b) states 59.0° Fahrenheit, which exactly matches the calculated result.  Given the calculation and comparison, it is clear that Output (b) accurately executes the instruction by providing the correct conversion of 15 degrees Celsius to Fahrenheit.  Therefore, Output (b) is better.|||Critic:As a Critic, I have reviewed the instruction, the two outputs, and the arguments presented by the General Public and the Scientist.
